    <li> Despite reading many negative reviews, I bought one and have had no problem. Works just like it claims. I suspect that the people who wrote the bad reviews either didn&#x27;t read the instructions or didn&#x27;t understand them.</li>
    <li> This is by far the best head shaver I&#x27;ve come across. I&#x27;ve shaved my head with clippers for the better part of 15 years and this all I need. The rounded blades work well with the contour of your head. I remove the guard to get the closest possible cut. The width of these clippers make it less likely that you miss a spot. Makes for a painless, easy and quick job. As long as you clean and oil it along with periodic charges it will last a long time. I would advise against leaving it on the charger continuously in between cuts, I feel like it shortens the battery life. Great shaver and it also helps with shaping my beard. Must buy.</li>
    <li> I have had this product for 3 months and in that time have given myself 5 haircuts. It works as described. It is quick and efficient, just remember to clean the comb often, like after every back and forth. It makes a big difference. I keep my hair at about a quarter of an inch, the #2 setting on the unit. I do find it takes multiple passes both side to side and front to back to get all the stray hairs. In my case maybe 10 minutes from start to finish. Keeping that 10 minutes in mind I have gotten 3 full haircuts out of one charge. After the third it was still running strong but I didn&#x27;t want to chance it running out of juice halfway through a fourth haircut. This unit combined with my Andis T-Outliner for the cleanup is simple to use (Have to recruit the wife to do around the ears) and it has paid for itself already compared to the barbershop.</li>

    <li> Tired of barbershops? I was when I bought this three years ago. I have now saved about three hundred bucks, and am just now having some battery issues because I left it discharged for a while. Don&#x27;t do that. This is the best of the personal hair trimmers I have used. It is so simple to just comb your hair and with the settings you can get it as short as you like. You will come to depend on this as I have, so take care of it. Remington really got this item right. Great gift item as well.</li>
    <li> The hair trimmer works just fine.  Its the charging unit that isn&#x27;t worth a plug nickel.  After about three charges it stopped charging.  I checked the charging unit and found that there was no output.  I bought another similar unit from Radio Shack and was able to again charge the unit.  I am aware that I could have returned it to Remington under the warranty but those things are more of a hassle than they are worth.  Perhaps Remington should find another vendor for their chargers.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As far as the unit is concerned, it performs exactly as I hoped it would.  I trim my hair every three to four days and it never looks as though it has grown.</li>
    <li> Edit 11-18-2009:  I&#x27;ve used this thing three times now and it&#x27;s worked very well each time.  That&#x27;s $60 in savings on hair cuts so far, so it&#x27;s more than paid for itself.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This thing really gets the job done once you get used to it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you currently have medium to long hair or if your hair is dense I highly recommend getting a haircut at a barber before you start using this thing.  Otherwise, you&#x27;re probably going to run out of battery power before you&#x27;re finished.  The battery on my Short Cut ran out just as I was finishing up the back.  I had charged it all night and all day (sixteen hours as recommended in the manual).  Yes, that&#x27;s right, when you buy this thing you have to charge it for a full sixteen hours before the first use to get maximum battery life.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I had medium to long hair when I started and the trimmer kept getting bogged down when I tried to comb it through my hair, so I had to make lots and lots and lots of passes to get it trimmed down to where the trimmer was fully functional even on the 4 setting (the longest setting).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What I love most about this thing is when I go to the barber they never cut my hair the way I want it cut -- they can only give me a \\&quot;number two\\&quot; or a \\&quot;number one\\&quot; etc. unless I go to an expensive stylist.  I&#x27;ll tell them \\&quot;I want a crew cut\\&quot; and they&#x27;ll trim off half an inch and go \\&quot;is that short enough\\&quot; and I&#x27;ll say \\&quot;no, shorter.  Crew cut.  Do you understand what that means?  I want it short, like an army haircut\\&quot; and they&#x27;ll start over and do the whole thing again, taking off another quarter inch until I get tired of asking and just go home with my hair longer than I want...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All I want is a short, \\&quot;crew cut,\\&quot; and this thing gives me exactly the cut I want.  It cuts all of my hair uniformly to the same length, all around.  For the cost I&#x27;m probably going to save a lot of money and annoyance.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As mentioned in the other reviews, you&#x27;ll want to get a trimmer for the sides and around the ears.  They can be had pretty cheap.  I didn&#x27;t try the one on the Short Cut but because of the shape of the Short Cut I decided it&#x27;d be too awkward and I might botch the job.  Speaking of botched jobs, you&#x27;ll want to have a few bucks on hand the first time you use this thing so you can go to the barber and have them fix it if you mess up too badly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Note that even though you can cut your own hair with this thing you&#x27;ll probably want to get someone else to trim up the back and behind your ears.  The first time I used it, I forgot I had taken off the adjustable comb and went to finish up the back, and cut a huge nick out of my hair down to the skin.  Fortunately it was far enough down that my roommate was able to use my trimmer to shore it up.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Finally, hair will go everywhere.  EVERYWHERE.  Fortunately hair is easy to vacuum up.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I&#x27;m happy with my sigourney-weavermatic.s and around the ears.  They can be had pretty cheap.     <li> For those, like me, who shave their head to the same short length, these clippers are very well designed.  The light feel and curved bi-directional blades make it a snap to cut my hair each week.  BUT...the battery is absolutely horrible.  It takes forever to charge and barely lasts one cut.  You can&#x27;t use the clippers with the cord attached so you are stuck having to charge overnight each time you plan to cut your hair.  Too bad about the battery because everything else seems to be designed to be used each week to keep your hair trimmed neatly.  But with the effort required to navigate around the battery&#x27;s shortcomings, it is nearly impossible to use it weekly.</li>
    <li> BUYER BEWARE! - You will see many reviewers on here giving reviews a few months after owning the product and most of them have pointed out that the unit dies.  It worked great for the first 2 months.  I loved it - it was cheap, and worked as advertised!  But after 4 months the unit would start shutting off about 45 seconds into cutting (after a FULL charge).  I found out I wasn&#x27;t the only one.    Why don&#x27;t they just let you plug it in and use it?  The \\&quot;cordless\\&quot; battery feature is not necessary (who cuts their hair where there is no power source?) and that feature is the reason it died.  The battery on this thing is useless and makes the product worthless.</li>

    <li> The Remington Short Cut Clipper is excellent for its stated purpose. As one who has recently decided to keep my hair trimmed very short, what some call a \\&quot;buzz-cut\\&quot; I have found it frustrating and tedious to maintain the cut with conventional hair clippers. I would miss places and would have to negotiate with the electrical cord in order to cut in all directions, since my hair wants to be curly when longer. With the Remington Short Cut Clipper I have attained an easy, brief daily maintenance device. It sits where my hair brush once resided, plugged in, fully charged and ready when I am at the basin doing my daily grooming, etc. I unplug it, check that the length setting is still where I left it last and then brush it back and forth over my scalp just as I would if I were brushing my hair. In about a minute and a half I am finished and I see an even cut all around.    I thoughtfully read product reviews as I decide whether to buy something I&#x27;ve not physically touched and examined. In this case I found some of the reviews to be confusing because of their negative ratings and the reasons for them. The Remington Short Cut Clipper is a device that is meant to be used for maintaining a very short \\&quot;buzz-cut\\&quot; and it does that very well.</li>
    <li> This product already has a ton of reviews, so I doubt mine will make a big difference.    The product works, as advertised. You can cut your own hair, without a mirror, easily and the results are great.    It may suck for long hair, but I don&#x27;t really care. My hair is SHORT and the more patchy and grey it becomes, the shorter it becomes.    Make sure you fully charge it and it will not run with the charger plugged in (odd?).    I use it like a toothbrush, cutting my hair every day. It is that easy.    Downside: no case, so I bought a small travel cube for storage.</li>
    <li> The cutters only take a little with each pass, so u have to go over and over and over to be sure you got a full and even cut so it takes a long time to do even a basic trim.     <li> The [[ASIN:B0015K9BXQ Remington Short Cut Cordless Haircut Kit]] is an excellent idea but the product just doesn&#x27;t deliver.  I was really hoping this was going to work for me.  Unfortunately, my experience with this product was mostly negative, and even for a minor trim around the sides I found this product to be poorly designed and without sufficient power.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I do think there are a select few who will be able to use this product.  If you have very fine hair, and tend to keep it between 1/2 inch and 1 inch long all around, this clipper can be a good supplement to normal hair-cuts.  I don&#x27;t think it sufficient to replace normal hair cuts for even this small group of consumers.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you have thicker or coarser hair that is longer than even 1 inch, this clipper is simply not powerful enough for giving yourself a trim.  Similarly, if you want to trim your hair down to the skin, even at the lowest setting this clipper cuts unevenly.  The problem is the blade angle, which is perpendicular to the scalp unlike a traditional clipper.  Combine that with the slower cutting action likely the result of this unit running off of a rechargeable battery.  The result is that it rarely cuts evenly and requires multiple passes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The size is adjustable by a dial on the inside of the handle that slides the guard farther or closer to the blade as you desire.  There are two guards included, one with plastic tabs that prevent you from dialing this down to the lowest length setting.  That one seems safer, but both guards seem impractical.  Neither of them gives you the option of having longer hair than most Wahl home kits.  I would estimate the longest length with this guard to be the equivalent of the 5 guard included with most home kits.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Hair also collects within the guard causing the clipper to get clogged re-cutting hair.  Having to remove this hair required me to remove the guard, slowing me down.  Even just trimming around the sides and back with this clipper was not practical because of the time needed to constantly clean hair out of guard.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Although I did notice that the battery wore down quickly, I never used it long enough to completely wear it out.  Most cordless rechargeable units have battery issues, so I would be willing to forgive that if not for the lack of power.  Those who keep their hair short all the time and don&#x27;t have thick hair like I do aer likely to be able to perform a quick trim on one charge.  It does seem to take a long time to fully charge.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The instructions were boiler-plate.  I didn&#x27;t see any instructions on how long the battery should be charged and how to extend battery life.  I will have to review the included manual, which has only a few pages of instructions in English and then duplicates them in Spanish and French.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you do end up getting it anyway, a few uses will be required in order to get the hang of it.  On a positive note, the shape of the unit seems very well designed for comfortable operation.  I will only add that you should make sure the blade is well oiled before use and that the unit is fully charged, as mine arrived with the battery drained.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;CONCLUSION&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For those with fine hair that is short to begin with, this can be a useful tool if used once a week so that the hair never gets too long.  For most people, the lack of power combined with design issues makes this product impractical.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Enjoy.because of the time needed to constantly clean hair out of guard. In addition, it has a push out trimmer that also works well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You can actually cut your hair without a mirror and I tend to go into the tub to cut my hair and then take a shower to wash all the loose hairs down the drain when I&#x27;m done (the clipper in not waterproof).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Because it is a small unit it doesn&#x27;t have the power to cut through long hair.  When my son wanted a haircut \\&quot;like dads,\\&quot; I first had to cut his hair down to size with traditional clippers and then I did the rest with the Remington.  Several neighbors commented how nice his hair looked!  In addition you have to occasionally \\&quot;tap out\\&quot; your hair from the cutting mechanism during a cut.  Lastly, the power switch is easy to accidently turn off when you are holding the unit.  All of these \\&quot;complaints\\&quot; are fairly trivial.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All in all, if you have a short \\&quot;buzz cut\\&quot; this device delivers at a reasonable price.  Definitely recommended.</li>

    <li> I was skeptical when I bought the Short Cut, apprehensive as hell the first time I took it to my head. No more. This thing is amazing! I used setting 3 on already short hair from a barbershop visit (my last, I think) 2 1/2 weeks ago. In 2-3 minutes, my hair looked exactly as it did when I last left the barber&#x27;s chair: Really short, cleanly cut, even all over.    Simple. Flawless. Even (dare I say?) FUN. I ran it slowly and steadily back and forth from front of head and down the back, then back the other direction, then ear to ear over the top, then back the other way, then along each side above the ears. You can use this baby about every 7-10 days (takes all of 2-3 minutes) and keep your hair exactly the length you want in perpetuity with nary the need for another time-consuming barbershop visit. Absolutely amazing. Now I&#x27;m thinking about going to a 2 and see what happens. I used setting 1 to trim the lower regions of my neck in the back and this seems to have worked well.     It seems that many of the gripes in this review section are from people who tried with little success to cut through long hair with it. The SC just is not designed for this. What it IS designed to do is keep already short hair short, or shorter.    What I did, and would suggest, is to visit the barber one more time and get your hair cut as short as you want, then when it just starts to get too long, go over it with the SC.    But, jeez, I just don&#x27;t see how anyone can screw it up.     Update, 8/1: I found that the best way to get a quick, even cut is to wash your hair, let it dry completely (about 3 minutes with super short hair), THEN use the short cut. This way your hair is straight up all over and doesn&#x27;t have a chance to get flattened anywhere on your head. Also, just spread a sheet of newspaper over the wash basin; this catches almost all the hair. Just fold it up and toss when you&#x27;re done. I&#x27;ve also done my cutting over the wash basin itself which seems to catch just about all the clippings. Then you just take a folded piece of toilet tissue, wet it lightly and scour the inside of the bowl. You get about 90% on the first pass, then use a dry sheet to clean up the rest. I&#x27;m really surprised at the some of the problems reported in the negative reviews. The whole process is about as simple and efficient as is realistically and reasonably possible.</li>

    <li> Inside the box:   Clipper, 2 attachment combs, charging adapter, cleaning brush, lubricating oil, and manual.     Review:  I bought this last summer because I thought it was an innovative hair clipper aimed at people who cut their own hair. However, tapering with this clipper is a little hard, so if you want to try styles other than a buzz cut, I would recommend getting the regular hair clippers from Andis or Oster.     I have very thick and straight Asian hair, and this clipper did a good job of cutting through my hair, but I had to do several passes to get the hair nice and even. It takes a while to charge, around 14-16 hours, and lasts about 30-40 minutes on a single charge. It does not run with the adapter plugged in, so if it should run out of battery while cutting your hair, you&#x27;re out of luck and will have to wait to at least partially charge it or resume the next day. I will note that it almost broke down on me once, when it would not turn on after a night of charging. I turned it on and off maybe 20 times before it started working.    The attachments are easily adjustable with a scrolling wheel but they do not conform perfectly to certain areas of my head, like the sides. There are two attachments, one balding attachment which cuts from 1/32\\&quot; (I do not know how long it can cut) and one adjustable guide comb which cuts from 1/8\\&quot; to 1/2\\&quot;. The manual says that it can be washed under water but it says to lubricate it with the provided oil afterward. I recommend lubricating with oil before every haircut as with other clippers.    Summary:    Pros:  -Easy, respectable self buzz cuts  -Cordless  -Easy adjustment of attachments  -Easy to hold while cutting hair  -Easy to maintain, just clean blades with supplied brush and lubricate    Cons:  -Mainly for buzz cuts. ades, crew cuts, etc    -Cannot be operated while plugged in   -When the battery dies, the whole clipper has to be replaced    In conclusion, buy this if all you&#x27;re looking for is a buzz cut. You can giveyourself a decent buzz cut in about 10 minutes. If you&#x27;re looking to try different hair styles, invest in a clipper like the Andis Improved master or Oster Fast Feed clippers.</li>

    <li> This is a great product. I used to cut my hair with a corded clipper. Easy enough process, with good results, but it would take about 10 minutes and I would have to pass over the same area multiple times. With this product, I can do a clean and short cut in less than three minutes and I do not need to do multiple passes. This makes keeping my haircut short, and at the length I like it, very, very easy. To anyone that likes a short and close haircut, this product is a must.</li>
    <li> PLEASE SEE MY UPDATE #2 at end of review for battery rejuvenation procedure.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Since I have a semi buzz cut style, it seemed increasingly silly to pay the barber $15 for the 5 minutes he spends on me.  I purchased this clipper for less than the cost of two \\&quot;professional\\&quot; haircuts.  It works well enough for me that I haven&#x27;t gone back to the barber, but there are certainly some areas for improvement.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1) The rechargeable batteries are non-replaceable, and they only last about a year or 10 recharges.  Therefore, you&#x27;ll have to buy an entirely new clipper every twelve months, or go through the warranty replacement hassle.  Still, $26 replacement cost per year beats 10 professional haircuts at $15 each ($150).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2) The little thumb dial that sets the haircut length does not have a firm notch for each setting.  Because it&#x27;s right under your finger in the natural grip position, it&#x27;s easy to accidentally twitch it during the course of a haircut, usually to a shorter setting.  And if you press the clipper against your head firmly, the cutter guides will \\&quot;collapse\\&quot; to a shorter setting.  So that&#x27;s two ways you can end up with a much shorter cut than you really wanted.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3) While cutting your hair, you must remember to hold the clipper at the same angle to your head all over your head. Hold it at a perpendicular right angle to your noggin.  If you tilt it back and forth as you run it around, the hair length becomes shorter as you tilt it more.  I suspect this is why some folks have complained about getting a \\&quot;patchy\\&quot; haircut, with various lengths in different areas of the head - they were tilting the cutter back and forth on different parts of their head.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4) With this clipper, you will still have difficulty creating a taper or sharp edge on the back of your neck.  I just live with it, but some people may not like that.  Or get your significant other to cut that last bit using the pop-up trimmer or the lowest setting on the hair length guide.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;By the way, I did, with great difficulty, disassemble the clipper in an attempt to replace the batteries.  However, the batteries are spot-welded to their connectors.  My past experience with trying to solder wires to batteries was unsuccessful, so I did not replace the batteries in this clipper.  (Short rant: I&#x27;m seeing far too many small consumer items which have non-replaceable batteries spot-welded in place.  I just threw away a $100 dollar ultrasonic toothbrush because the batteries were dead and welded in place.  This is not environmentally nor consumer friendly - why should I toss 100&#x27;s of dollars worth of electronic parts in the landfill just because the batteries, which could be replaced for less than $5, are welded permanently in place. And to add insult to injury, these appliances - like this clipper - will not run and perform their function when plugged into the charger.  So once the battery is dead, you can&#x27;t even choose to use it in the plugged in mode.  Frankly, I think this kind of non-replaceable battery design should be illegal, for environmental protection reasons.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m giving it three stars because it&#x27;s the only product like this available.  If somebody came out with a similar curved edge clipper design with replaceable batteries, able to run while plugged in and has a more reliable hairlength control, I&#x27;d switch to that product - and I&#x27;d come back here and reduce this rating to 1 or 2 stars.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&gt;&gt; UPDATE &amp;lt;&amp;lt;&lt;br /&gt;Well, it&#x27;s now 9 months after my review.  I&#x27;ve used the Remington about once every two weeks during that period, for 5 minutes at a time.  That&#x27;s 18 times or 90 minutes of running time, always recharged between each use.  The clipper has now become useless, incapable of running for more than 30 seconds when fully charged. So I saved the cost of 12 haircuts, 12 times $15 is $180.  That&#x27;s $180 I saved with this $26 purchase.  While it&#x27;s very annoying that the batteries in this device are sopoor and non-replaceable, the return on investment is pretty good and I&#x27;ll probably buy another to replace this one.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&gt;&gt; IMPORTANT UPDATE #2 &amp;lt;&amp;lt;&lt;br /&gt;Now it&#x27;s 12 months after purchase.  I&#x27;ve discovered that you can substantially rejuvenate the batteries by occasionally COMPLETELY discharging them before recharging.  This is contrary to the manufacturers instructions, which claim it&#x27;s OK to leave the device plugged into the charger permanently.  Instead, I now occasionally turn the cutter on and leave it running until it&#x27;s completely discharged and stops running.  I let it sit for 1/2 an hour, then I turn it on AGAIN and leave it running.  I keep doing this, over and over again, until finally it will no longer come on even briefly.  Then I give it a full overnight charge.  The result is that it will now run for 8-12 minutes rather than 30 seconds, and that&#x27;s more than enough time to give myself a haircut.  So my advice - about every fourth haircut, you must give the batteries a completely thorough discharge in order to rejuvenate their recharge life.  It might even make sense to rejuvenate the batteries soon after you first receive a new cutter, since apparently there are a lot of these cutters that have been sitting in warehouses for years, slowly draining the batteries.d I&#x27;ll probably buy another to replace this one.    &gt;&gt; IMPORTANT UPDATE #2 &lt;&lt;  Now it&#x27;s 12 months after purchase.  I&#x27;ve discovered that you can substantially rejuvenate the batteries by occasionally COMPLETELY discharging them before recharging.  This is contrary to the manufacturers instructions, which claim it&#x27;s OK to leave the device plugged into the charger permanently.  Instead, I now occasionally turn the cutter on and leave it running until it&#x27;s completely discharged and stops running.  I let it sit for 1/2 an hour, then I turn it on AGAIN and leave it running.  I keep doing this, over and over again, until finally it will no longer come on even briefly.  Then I give it a full overnight charge.  The result is that it will now run for 8-12 minutes rather than 30 seconds, and that&#x27;s more than enough time to give myself a haircut.  So my advice - about every fourth haircut, you must give the batteries a completely thorough discharge in order to rejuvenate their recharge life.  It might even make sense to rejuvenate the batteries soon after you first receive a new cutter, since apparently there are a lot of these cutters that have been sitting in warehouses for years, slowly draining the batteries.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve read the reviews good and bad, and decided to purchase it anyway because the method of \\&quot;combing\\&quot; with this clipper seemed like it would be a much more natural action than trimming with normal hair-clippers. The caveat is that it is a great tool for maintaining the length of a short haircut, but but not such a great tool for cutting hair that is not already in a crew cut. You will need a conventional clipper or a trip to the barber to start out.    When I received it, I plugged it in to charge a whole day before use. Upon initial turn-on the motor started with an enthusiastic buzz, but then dropped in pitch and held a steady, but lower, speed. I initially thought that perhaps I had a unit with a bad battery that would not hold a charge, however I&#x27;ve used it extensively for a few weeks and it always keeps going for as long as I&#x27;ve needed to run it. I guess it just starts up \\&quot;fast\\&quot;, but the lower steady speed is the normal speed.    I&#x27;m happy that I can do a really quick trim to maintain my haircut once or more each week. It is cordless, so I can do this in the shower-stall (without water) to contain the mess and then just rinse away the trimmings, which are no bigger than shaving stubble. In sum, I recommend this trimmer 100% for maintaining an existing crew-cut.</li>

    <li> I saw an ad in a magazine for the Short Cut and thought it would be perfect for me. I&#x27;ve been buzzing my head for about a year now and I use no attachments so its as short as it gets without using a razor. I tried the Short Cut out this morning for the first time and I&#x27;ll give it an A- overall.     It did seem to come with some sort of charge but I charged it overnight to be safe, didn&#x27;t want to run out of battery halfway. As others may have pointed out be aware that the attachment installed when you first open it is the &#x27;balding&#x27; attachment which will have no change if you set the adjustable numbers higher, its for super short only. Normally I cut my hair about every 5 days. I sometimes do it more often but waiting a few days in between makes it easier to see what&#x27;s been cut and what hasn&#x27;t. I used the Short Cut this morning after about 3 and a half days or growth. Overall impression is it works very well. Being that I wasn&#x27;t taking much length off it did take a few more passes than normal to get everything but it definitely does clip on both the back and forth movements. What I really liked is there seemed to be no way to cut myself which is a constant worry with regular clippers. It took a couple minutes to figure out the best angle to get all parts of my head; some parts cut better front to back, some side to side. It just depends on the way your hair grows. What threw me off at first is it doesn&#x27;t make as much &#x27;grinding&#x27; noise as its cutting. Its quieter overall which is nice, although the &#x27;grinding&#x27; sound is usually my audible confirmation that I definitely cut a patch of hair. The front and sides cut pretty easily but where this thing really shines is in back. It only took me about 20 seconds to do the whole back of my head. With regular clippers I&#x27;d do the back and then have to spot check with a mirror.    The only real problem I had was with my sideburns. Maybe its just the shape of my head but I couldn&#x27;t get it to sit low enough to get them. I eventually found a way of doing it but it put the Short Cut dangerously close to my eyebrows so I&#x27;ll have to be really careful. There is another small flat trimmer that pops out of the top but it seems to be a little shorter than the curved blade so it might make my sideburns a tad too short, I&#x27;ll experiment next time.    Just for comparison I whipped out my old clippers to see how close the Short Cut actually cuts. The clippers did cut a tiny bit shorter but it was totally negligible, the hair that fell into the sink was as thin as powder so the Short Cut seems to trim just as short.     Pros:  -cordless  -curved blades hug my head well and cut both back and forth  -30 minutes of runtime is adequate for a couple uses before recharging  -nicking yourself is almost impossible  -fits very well in my hand    Cons:  -some places are hard to reach with curved blade  -needs to be shaken out once a minute or so, the hair tends to fall in instead of out as you cut so it can get clogged up but a quick shake or tap clears it out.  -no carry case included  -relatively long charge time (says 14-16 hours for full recharge)    Overall I like it and I&#x27;ll use it from now on. The small size and cordless power is especially nice for traveling too :)</li>

    <li> EDIT: **TWO years of weekly use and still works as new!!** Remember to oil before each use and thoroughly clean with a brush after. And always fully charge before using. Would love to see Remington to release a new model with USB charging of this item (They have it in other models).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;ORIGINAL REVIEW:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After the mixed reviews, I waited for a year and about 40 uses to write mine.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I use this clipper every weekend, at 1, 1.5, 2 or 3, depending on the mood. Usually 1.5. In my case it works great, I have very thick hair and the blades chop it without problem. However, if I let my hair grow a bit more that the usual (2-3 weeks) and I want to use the shortest sizes, the clipper will have a hard time (And so do I), but in the end it can do the work.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Regarding the maintenance I have found out that:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1) You need to charge it ALWAYS. The motor requires the battery to be in its top capacity. I tried using the clipper until it really needed recharging but the motor couldn&#x27;t keep working. ALWAYS CHARGE the clipper after using it. Because the battery is Lithium-Ion it can hold the charge adequately for at least a week in my case.&lt;br /&gt;2) Also, ALWAYS clean and oil the clipper: Before using it I add a drop or two of oil for each centimeter along the blades. After using it I take a small brush, take out the guide and brush it through. I haven&#x27;t even gone through half the oil bottle included, a recommended replacement would be 3-in-1.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There are some cons, one is the charging adapter, it is 120V only, if I need to travel to somewhere else where the voltage is 100V or 220/240V, it will not work. This isn&#x27;t a travel friendly item. (However Remington has a USB rechargeable clipper on their catalog!). Also it doesn&#x27;t let to use the clipper while charging. The battery isn&#x27;t replaceable.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Everything taken into account, this is a great item, for me it only needs a 100-240V international adapter, a replaceable battery andit will be even better.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I wrote to Remington about the adapter, they just said something along the lines of \\&quot;Buy another one wherever you go\\&quot;. I found, after solder-sucking the old dead nimh cell, that there are any number of battery upgrades on the market that are in the correct spec range for this unit, priced from 3-10 dollars.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I did not re-solder my new Eneloop battery. Just stretch-taped the contacts to the wires and tacked the thing in place with a bit of sticky gel, then snapped the unit back together. My cost for battery surgery was about 3 bucks and 40 minutes&#x27; labor. It will take 15 minutes next time, now that I know what I&#x27;m doing.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As for usage, I&#x27;m with the other reviewers. It works well once you settle on a style you can live with and learn to do it right. I&#x27;ve now been a DIY hair cutter for going on a year, and I don&#x27;t expect I&#x27;ll pay someone for another haircut unless this tool or one like it becomes unavailable.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Batteries are no longer a limiting factor. Mechanically my year-old Shortcut works pretty much like it did new. When it dies I&#x27;ll happily buy another just like it.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve owned this product for almost 6 months now and I&#x27;ve been very happy with it. No fuss and very easy to use.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Regarding the battery: I suspect that this device uses Nickel Cadmium batteries. Because of this, I make sure to fully discharge it before my next charge (that is, the low battery indicator lights up AND the clipper turns off a couple seconds after I try to turn it on). If I don&#x27;t do this, my clipper&#x27;s battery will experience the \\&quot;memory effect\\&quot; which is inherent in nickel cadmium (or similar) based batteries. I make sure to avoid overcharging it as well as it might experience the \\&quot;lazy effect\\&quot; which is, again, inherent in nickel cadmium batteries.</li>

    <li> remington short-cut easy to use for those with already short hair...handles like a brush and in a few short minutes you have a very professional looking cut...</li>
    <li> I tried this product out on my two year-old son at first.  He had been getting buzz cuts from the Hair Butchery for a while and he basically screamed bloody murder every time we went in there.  I got tired of hearing it and paying good money to do so.  I had also been \\&quot;entertaining\\&quot; the idea of that hairstyle (if it can be called that) for myself.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I saw it on sale and with a rebate which brought the total price down to $19.99.  I got it home and touched up his little punkin head.  I wish I had read the instructions that said the balding comb was attached from the factory.  But other than a little bitty bald spot on the back of his skull, no harm was done.  It actuaally cleaned up his &#x27;do pretty good.  Subsequent uses have honed my skills and he&#x27;s looking pretty sharp if I should say so myself.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I threw caution to the wind yesterday and did my own.  I guess it looks OK since my wife didn&#x27;t laugh hysterically or run out of the room when I came downstairs. Feels pretty good now, that&#x27;s for sure.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One caveat though; take your time. And if you have a full head of hair to start with like I did, be patient and keep at it.  Or you can go one last time to your barber or stylist and tell them it&#x27;s goodbye.  But wait until after they cut your hair...</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve been cutting my own hair for 15 years... ever since a particularly bad haircut from a barber in 1993.  I don&#x27;t use anything except a standard Conair-type clipper and the trimmer function on the back of my electric razor.  The whole process is a little time consuming and there are many times when I make blind cuts, which is basically using my fingers to determine length while not being able to see any of the action.    When I saw this Remington Short Cut Clipper online I thought I might have stumbled into a perfect solution for my hair cutting needs.  The design is very innovative, allowing for cutting with either hand that goes more quickly because the blades are wider and they&#x27;re shaped to follow the contour of the head.    After receiving the product and trying it on my own hair, I have to give it just an average rating.  Here is what the Remington does right:    1.  The fact that it&#x27;s cordless is a huge plus.  No cords get in the way, which has always been an issue with traditional clippers.  2.  The bi-directional cutting is wonderful, and combined with the ambidextrous design this makes the clipper equally useful in either hand and in both directions.  3.  The pop-up trimmer is the perfect size to trim around the ears.  It is longer and narrower than typical back-of-the-electric razor trimmers, which makes the hard-to-reach places and angles much easier to navigate.    Here are the issues I have with the Remington:    1.  Unless you want a true short-all-over cut, this clipper isn&#x27;t for you.  My hair is longer on the top, but very short on the sides and in the back.  I like to start short on the bottom and then blend it with longer hair as I move up.  That strategy doesn&#x27;t work well with this trimmer.  My personal attempt resulted in choppy cuts that had to be smoothed over with regular clippers.  2.  The contour shape of the plastic length attachment and the blades are only good for the round parts of your head.  The sides of my head don&#x27;t happen to bulgeout in a rounded fashion, so it made trimming the sides of my hair very difficult.  Navigating around the ears was also trouble.  3.  The plastic attachment quickly fills up with cut hair and needs to be emptied.  I would prefer that it just fell off and didn&#x27;t accumulate in the clipper.    Maybe I am not the intended user for this product.  If I just wore buzz cuts or crew cuts, this product would get 5 stars from me.  With that type of haircut, you really will get a quick and clean cut.  But I think others like me would appreciate a little more flexibility in dealing with blending slightly longer hair.</li>
    <li> The devil is in the details, or so the saying goes. With the RSCC, Satan&#x27;s been forced out of the hair-cutting business.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Over the years, I&#x27;ve become a proponent of self-cut short hair. It&#x27;s easier to manage and I don&#x27;t have to deal with barbers who no longer want to be called barbers but aesthetes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The normal clippers I use while perfectly adequate always seem to leave a section of hair longer or shorter than others. This is very frustrating. The Short Cut Clipper cuts hair perfectly to the same desired length with every pass. The design of it means I can hold it like a comb and move it through the hair as with a comb.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The curved cutting clippers that can be raised and lowered with a clicker setting combined with a guard ensures the DIY barber will not be able to give himself (or herself?) a bad haircut. Highly recommended and a joy to own.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;**Update (6/22/2009): Using the Remington Short Cut continues to be a pleasure however, I have finally found one shortcoming: the build-up of hair in the  teeth and comb of the implement really impedes continued hair-cutting past a few (2 or 3) minutes. This would have brought down the star rating from 5 to 4 or 4.5.</li>

    <li> There is a recurring theme in these reviews. Users complain that this clipper loses its battery capacity. They conclude this because the clipper bogs down during a clip session - the motor slows down and eventually stops.  I was having the same problem and figured the clipper was a lemon. But I went back and started re-reading the reviews here to see what others had experienced.  I found one review where the reviewer claimed he had brought his clipper back to life by lubricating it with clipper oil. I had some clipper oil in the house and figured it was worth a shot.  And presto! A few drops of clipper oil on the blades and the clipper came back to life. In fact it was actually working better than when it was new. It maintained full speed throughout the cut, which it had not done since a month after I bought it.  I now put a couple of drops of clipper oil on the blades before each use. The clipper works beautifully. I clip down to stubble once a week. The clipper does a very fast and complete job. The curved shape really speeds the process up compared with flat clippers.   I am now a very satisfied customer.  I use [[ASIN:B000B9SFQG Wahl 4-Ounce Blade Oil]] but I&#x27;m sure any clipper oil would work.</li>

    <li> I have used the Remington Short Cut Clipper for five years.  My first lasted forty months, until the battery would no longer charge.  Spreading the purchase price of (then) $24.95 over 40 months, it cost just 0.63 cents per haircut .  I keep mine plugged in all the time, when not in use, and this may or may not prolong battery life (I haven&#x27;t identified the type of battery, in order to determine best practice for charging).  Regardless, this clipper is a great way to cut your hair without the risk of making an accidental divot.  It takes me about fifteen to twenty minutes to cut my hair--far less time than it would take to drive to a barber shop, wait my turn, and receive a haircut.  If you value self-sufficiency, this a great tool!  I keep one active and one in reserve. I haven&#x27;t had the negative experiences reported by some owners, but do want to echo reports that the clipper comes with the &amp;#34;balding attachment&amp;#34; installed, rather than the adjustable comb. Make sure to swap the adjustable comb for the &amp;#34;balding&amp;#34; attachment unless you want a &amp;#34;buzz cut&amp;#34;.  I recommend this product without reservation.</li>

    <li> The Remington \\&quot;Short Cut\\&quot;  hair clipper is, just as the name implies, for short haircuts. I had been considering going to a shorter style for a while, and thought this would be a good opportunity to move in that direction. So I gave it a shot and was pleased with the result.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The longest finished length this clipper will allow is somewhere between  and  inch. The adjustable length comb has  inch teeth, but the curved blade comes up into the teeth some way, making the finished length of the hair less than the length of the teeth. The depth of cut is controlled by a thumb wheel.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Do not try to use this clipper if your hair has any length at all. If your hair is long enough to fall over on its own the clipper will just bend it over and won&#x27;t effectively cut it. It is obviously intended to give an even trim to very short hair styles, with the hair standing up as it passes the blade.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As others have noted, this clipper will not take you to a short hairstyle, but it will very effectively maintain one. If you have longer hair, your best bet is to go to a stylist for the initial cut and use the trimmer to maintain the look. While it won&#x27;t replace professional haircuts, it will reduce the need for them from 8 to 12 times a year to one or two.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The extendable trimmer works well for cleaning up edges and mowing around ears and other obstructions. You are still going to want somebody to help even-up things in the back for you.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The unit is relatively quiet, does not heat up like many clippers do, and fully charges in about 14-hours. One charge is plenty to complete a good trimming.  The teeth and blade are removable for cleaning and the instructions say the unit can be immersed in water for cleaning (although I didn&#x27;t try it).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You will want to do the trimming with a towel or other \\&quot;drop cloth\\&quot; around your shoulders and quite a few fine trimmings will end-up on the floor.  When all is said and done the Remington Short Cut Clipper does the job, and will pay for its self with just a few missed haircuts.y for its self with just a few missed haircuts.</li>

The curved blade that is so nice for the back and top of the head is useless on the side of your head just above the ears.  This is the most important area for me to shave down because hair over my ears drives me crazy.  Think about how a curved blade is supposed to get that area.  It can&#x27;t go vertical because your ear is in the way.  It can&#x27;t go horizontal because my head isn&#x27;t rounded there.  Maybe my head is the wrong shape, but it didn&#x27;t work for me.    Flaw #2: \\&quot;Tracks\\&quot;.  If you&#x27;ve used a clipper before, you&#x27;ve probably seen the comb tracks left behind when using an attachment.  Usually, I go over the tracks in different directions to even everything out.  I could not get rid of the tracks using this Clipper.  I looked like my head was striped!  Maybe if I shaved to the lowest setting the tracks would go away?    So, after having two flaws that made these clippers basically useless to me, why three-stars?  Because they work if you are looking for a longer cut.  I used this at the \\&quot;2\\&quot; setting on my son and it cleaned him up nicely.  The design and ease of use are really nice - I just wish it worked better on me.    BOTTOM LINE: If you&#x27;re looking to clean up some straggling hairs on a longer crew/buzz cut - this could be the tool for you.  Using it like a brush is a real time saver.  If you&#x27;re looking to go real short, I would have to recommend you stick with a traditional clipper (such as [[ASIN:B000MND29Q Conair HCT475 Rechargeable Cord/Cordless Pro Style  Kit, 24 Piece]] ).  I always end up using them to clean up after failed attempts with other clippers/razors.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve been using this product for the past three months, and I couldn&#x27;t be more pleased.  It produces the same quality haircut as the barber shop, and it&#x27;s as quick and convenient as shaving.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have to admit, I did not have high expectations when I ordered this product from Amazon.  After it arrived, it took me another month to work up the courage to use it.  Finally, on the first day of my vacation, when I knew I would have time to grow out my hair a bit if the clipper made a mess of things, I took the plunge.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It turns out that the clipper is incredibly easy to use.  Because of the curved design and bidirectional cutters, the optimal motion is very similar to shaving.  You just \\&quot;comb\\&quot; the clipper back and forth around your head until you&#x27;ve covered all areas.  It&#x27;s amazingly simple and produces very even results.  You can literally use it with your eyes closed.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have not had the problem noted by another reviewer of clogged blades.  I keep my hair trimmed short (about 1/4 inch, or the No. 2 comb on a traditional hair clipper), and the short hairs just fall away.  I suspect that this trimmer is really only suitable for short hair.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Two issues you should note, though:&lt;br /&gt;1) The trimmer comes from the factory with the balding comb attached.  You need to pop it off and replace it with the comb that let&#x27;s you set hair length.  This is a silly way to ship the clipper -- unless you read the instructions carefully, you might miss this important detail and end up with an essentially shaved head.  Remington should ship it with the safer comb and let you switch to the balding comb.&lt;br /&gt;2) The trimmer doesn&#x27;t have a battery gauge like many shavers, and it cannot run directly off AC power (it won&#x27;t turn on when plugged into the charger).  This can be inconvenient if the trimmer runs out of power half way through a haircut.  I&#x27;ve made it a habit to charge the trimmer once a month whether it needs it or not.  A batter gauge would be nice. [Update 19 March 2011: The clipper is now about 2 1/2 years old, and the batteries don&#x27;t seem to hold a charge as well any more. The clipper still works fine, but now I need to charge it after every use, or the battery dies half way through the next haircut. I wish the batteries were replaceable. I bought another one last month in case the batteries on the original fail completely.]&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Bottom line:  This clipper has exceeded my expectations.  It allows me to cut my own (admittedly short) hair at home as easily as shaving, rather than having to make trips to the barber shop.  It has already paid for itself, let&#x27;s me cut my hair more frequently (and therefore avoid the \\&quot;hey, you got your hair cut\\&quot; syndrome when I&#x27;d let it get too long before cutting), and is super convenient.  What a nice surprise.s now about 2 1/2 years old, and the batteries don&#x27;t seem to hold a charge as well any more. The clipper still works fine, but now I need to charge it after every use, or the battery dies half way through the next haircut. I wish the batteries were replaceable. I bought another one last month in case the batteries on the original fail completely.]    Bottom line:  This clipper has exceeded my expectations.     <li> I&#x27;ve been cutting my own hair for well over a decade now, ever since it started receding and I decided that paying someone [...] bucks a month to cut it was foolish. This is the fastest, easiest, most worry-free clippers I have ever used. I used to have my wife inspect my head after cutting because I inevitably missed a spot, but because of the bi-directional cutting it is easy to get every last hair. I love the bald cut, and because it is so quick to maintain after the first time, I can cut my hair in minutes, a couple times a week, with minimal clean up. My only complaint is that you cannot use it corded when the battery gets low, but that is a minor inconvenience. I would recommend this clipper to anyone who likes to keep their hair short (there is a longer length comb included) with minimal fuss and repeatable results.</li>

    <li> The first thing that you should know about this clipper is that it&#x27;s called the \\&quot;Shortcut\\&quot; for a reason, the reason being that it only works if you want a buzz cut with your scalp showing.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The second thing is that you should read the instructions before using it.     <li> I buy way too many \\&quot;gadgets\\&quot;.  Most of them sound like cool toys and usually end up at the bottom of a drawer or in the trash.  Of the gadgets I&#x27;ve bought that I can&#x27;t live without, regardless of the price I paid, are my GPS unit, phone headset, Tivo and a handful of others.  The first time I saw the Remington ShortCut hair trimmer I didn&#x27;t think twice about it and walked away.  It is a gadget that&#x27;s designed for a very limited and specialized target market ... those who like to have their hair cut very short and evenly across their entire head.  It&#x27;s also a gadget that has zero necessity, because there are all kinds of hair clippers on the market, and only a small percentage of people cut their own hair.  So I thought the idea was silly.  Then I started looking at my hair in the mirror and noticed that there are always some wayward strands that grow faster and make my haircut look less-than-fresh.  And, to get away with the close-cropped look, it really has to be trimmed every few days to keep it even and orderly.  That would get pretty spendy at a barber shop.  What I&#x27;ve been doing until I discovered the Remington ShortCut is to use regular electric barber clippers with one of those cheesy plastic guides that is supposed to cut your hair at an even length.  It is definitely not easy to use single-handedly and the length of my hair after clipping is always just a tiny bit too short.  With low expectations I tried the ShortCut.  My first impression is that it has a pretty good build quality.  It comes pre-installed with the balding comb.  CAUTION:  if you don&#x27;t want to look like an egg after your first trim, be sure to take the balding comb off and replace it with the adjustable comb!  The adjustable comb has 5 preset stops ranging from about \\&quot; to about \\&quot;.  What Remington doesn&#x27;t say is that you can really set it to anywhere in between if you are careful not to press it too hard against your scalp (which you shouldn&#x27;t do anyway).  After charging the unit overnight I was anxious to try it and swiped it a few times casually over my head.  I was impressed.  With a few simple motions, the same as using a hairbrush, the job was done and my hair was very neatly trimmed, with no pesky strands of longer-than-usual hairs poking out.  A few minutes every few days is all it takes to have your hair perfectly trimmed 24/7.  In my judgment, that is what make a product a necessity rather than a gadget, and makes it worth whatever price you pay.  Except the price for the ShortCut is dirt cheap.  This is one of the most highly recommended items I&#x27;ve reviewed and earns a solid 5 stars.  For maybe 95% of people, they would have no need for the ShortCut, but for me and guys like the new U.S. president it is a total winner.ht I was anxious to try it and swiped it a few times casually over my head. I clipped my hair to a #4 length- I had longer hair to begin with. Ideally this is used for short hair to maintain it. It is not particularly powerful, so if your hair is grown out like mine was, it will take quite a few back and fourths to get rid of the hair- not to mention tapping out the clipper when it gets clogged up every 5 or so passes. However.... This is still a great deal, and already saved me money. you still need a mirror set to get the back line right on your head, and I brought in my girlfriend to touch up some spots on the back and by my ears. In any case, if this thing even lasts 4 hair cuts, I am way in the green. My hair cut came out as good as super cuts etc. and I can maintain it at this length now. 5 stars when they come out with plug-in-able version. You will need a full charge to get through a tougher hair cut. Very easy to adjust lengths, and comes with two guards (one is like a #.5-2.5, ad the other is up to a #4) The guards clip in and out easy, and this thing is light and feels like you are brushing your hair. Overall a good do for the short hair-types.</li>

    <li> Let me start by addressing the elephant in the room, the battery. I was very hesitant to buy the Remington Short Cut because of the large number of negative reviews about the battery. I&#x27;m glad I decided to buy it anyway.  My experience with the battery so far has not been a negative one.  The first time I charged the Short Cut I left it plugged in overnight. When the unit is charged the blue light will go out. I get about two 10-12 minute trims on a single charge with about two weeks between trims, so I end up charging the Short Cut about once a month. I always charge it the day before I need to use it and never after the battery is run down after performing a cut. While I can&#x27;t speak about the longevity of the battery, I can say that I am happy that I don&#x27;t need to charge the Short Cut every time I use it. I think the longer you go between charges may extend the overall life of the battery as well.   Update:  I used my Short Cut this morning (7/5/15) and decided I would update my Amazon review. To my surprise I checked my purchase history and I purchased my Short Cut on 6/27/13 and it is still going strong, and I mean strong. I typically use it 2-3 time as month and charge it about every 2 weeks. I think the key to longer battery life is cleanliness. I thoroughly clean and oil the blades each use. At first I wasn&#x27;t oiling the blades after each use but I noticed an audible difference in the sound after oiling. It sounds smoother and less worked when oiled regularly. This thing has saved me well over $200 and I would definitely buy another one once the battery on the one I own now dies. Right now it is not showing any sign of it.  OK, on to the rest of my review. The very first time I cut my hair with the Short Cut I was very nervous. I have always had my hair cut by someone else my entire life so the thought of doing it myself was rather daunting the first time. However, the product&#x27;s box is correct: You can&#x27;t mess this up! You literally use the Short Cut like a comb and it does all the work for you. The whole process is pretty messy so you better have a towel wrapped around your neck. I quickly learned the best place to cut my hair is in the shower before taking a shower. When I&#x27;m done I clean the Short Cut and after taking a shower I don&#x27;t have the irritating feeling of hair on my neck and shoulders. The end result is a nice even short cut hair cut.  A few other things about the Short Cut. It comes with two guards, oil, and a cleaning brush. The first time I plugged it in to charge it the blue light came on and when I checked it the next morning (less than 10 hours later) the blue light was out. Initially I thought something was wrong but this is a normal indication.  The Short Cut comes with two guards. One guard is primarily for bald cuts while the other guard lets you choose an adjustable length cut be turning a wheel on the Short Cut which adjusts the guard up and down. A word of caution: When changing the guard or removing the guard to clean the Short Cut, adjust the guard up to the highest setting and gently remove the guard. The guards are keyed which make putting it back on a breeze. Again, use the highest setting when removing or changing the guard.  There are a few things I don&#x27;t like about the Short Cut. First, the Short Cut does not come with any kind of storage bag, but I did find that everything fits nicely into a gallon zip lock bag. The Short Cut has a built in pop out trimmer but it does not work very well. Honestly, it was a big let down the first time I tried to use it to trim my sideburns and around my ears. It just doesn&#x27;t really feel like it is cutting anything.  This is the main reason I give it 4 instead of 5 stars.  Overall, I would highly recommend the Short Cut for anyone who likes a short buzz cut. For years and years I paid on average $10-12 for a buzz cut about once a month. With the Short Cut I am able to maintain my short cut by using it about three times a month. I cannot tell the differencebetween a professional $10-12 cut and the Short Cut cut. The $29.99 I paid for the Short Cut has already paid for itself. The Short Cut literally feels like you are brushing your hair, it&#x27;s that easy. No matter what direction you are brushing, the Short Cut is cutting your hair. The more you use the Short Cut the more comfortable it feels cutting your own hair. If you like your hair short and  looking for a way to maintain a good looking hair cut and save money to boot, the Short Cut is worth a look.  You really can&#x27;t mess this up!</li>

    <li> I stand by this product, as it has saved me countless dollars per use.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is the second one I&#x27;ve bought(first time through Amazon) in the past since 2008 or so if i recall. The first one couldn&#x27;t hold the charge anymore, due to what I believe was poor storage management.  As I would usually leave it plugged in for recharge in the bathroom where there&#x27;s constant moisture and leave it alone till I&#x27;m ready to use it again in 3 weeks or so.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A little back story why I&#x27;ve bought this...Like many men, I&#x27;m starting to gradually lose hair.  And going to the barber has become, embarrassing sort of speak.  With this, I&#x27;ve been able to save the thought of believing that other people even bother to think what I look like, but it&#x27;s just that much more comforting knowing you don&#x27;t have to doubt yourself.  A typical trip to the barber will run me around $15 + tip, and that at least saved me $1,000 over the years.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now on to how I use this.  There&#x27;s pretty much only 2 hair styles a person using this product can do by themselves.  1 - all around even cut or 2 - cut the sides short and leave the top longer with some scissors for room to style.  I will have to say, the first time using these clippers, I was inexperienced and it looked hideous.  But with practice comes perfection.  No one is perfect their first time so they might mark it off as a mistake.  But once you get a routine down, in 10 minutes you&#x27;ll have a style you&#x27;re accustomed to.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When I cut my hair, I lean over the tub. Make sure to use the default comb.&lt;br /&gt;1. Have the clippers on setting 2.&lt;br /&gt;2. Start with the back and go back and forth until the hair is clean.  Some tapping on the clipper may be required to remove the hair depending on how long your hair is.&lt;br /&gt;3. After that I proceed with the sides.&lt;br /&gt;4. Once that&#x27;s done, setting 1.5 on the back and work my way up from the bottom to maybe earlobe height.&lt;br /&gt;Set it to 1 and cover half way of the 1.5 setting.&lt;br /&gt;5.Set it to 3 and cut the rim between the sides and top.&lt;br /&gt;6. Depending what you want, it&#x27;s your choice to go from there.  But I highly suggest using the same comb filter on 4 setting and just clip it through to see how it looks on you.&lt;br /&gt;7. Use the slider to clip the hair around your ears that the normal clipper couldn&#x27;t get to.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;And that&#x27;s it!</li>
